Chiang Orders Construction of Fortifications in Safe Zones to Prevent Bandits 108

| Constructing Pillboxes to Prevent Bandit Surprise Attacks |

Nanchang dispatch: Chairman Chiang, regarding the plan to suppress bandits, previously ordered all counties and districts to build more pillboxes and defend key points, so that even a small number of troops could provide long-term defense. However, various places either claimed to be far from the bandit areas or cited financial difficulties as reasons, and mostly outwardly complied but inwardly disobeyed this construction. Chiang recently ordered all provinces that all safe zones within 240 li of bandit areas must build pillboxes to prevent bandits. The key points of his instruction are: (1) Various places often think that having a city means that there is no need to build pillboxes, but they do not know that old cities require many soldiers to defend and are not easy to defend. Often with more troops, if there are points, such as on the city walls or outside the city, that can overlook the city or form a mutual defense, building one or two pillboxes will allow even a small number of troops to defend for a long time. (2) Various places often cite financial difficulties as a reason, but they should know that being captured once will result in losses that are more than double. (3) Various places often think that because they are safe zones, there is no need to build pillboxes, but they should know that roaming bandits can travel hundreds of li in a day and night. How can they not take precautions in advance? From now on, all cities and towns within 240 li of bandit areas must construct pillboxes and prepare accordingly. The commanders of the stationed troops and the provincial government should supervise at all times. (January 10th)

Page 9

The Naval Recovery of Xiamen 109

Huang Qiang Expressed Willingness to Concede in Advance

Lin and Du Jointly Maintain Order

Xiamen dispatch: Xiamen Naval Port Commander Lin Guogeng and Military Affairs Committee Fujian Military Special Envoy Du Qiyun recovered Xiamen in one night on the 9th without causing alarm, ensuring the safety of Chinese and foreign civilians. The following is a record of the situation.

Previously, at the beginning of the Fujian Incident, Cai Tingkai appointed Huang Qiang as the Zhangzhou-Xiamen Garrison Commander and sent him to Xiamen to establish a command headquarters. Huang was originally ordered to take over the Xiamen fortress and gun emplacements, but at that time, Xiamen was garrisoned by a marine corps regiment and two regiments of the 19th Route Army's 335th regiment. If the takeover were implemented, war would certainly break out. To avoid war, the naval port headquarters would not withdraw. Huang, fearing causing a war, and Naval Port Commander Lin Guogeng, through the mediation of the consular corps, agreed that the marine corps and the 19th Route Army would each withdraw two battalions, leaving one battalion each in Xiamen to maintain the status quo. When the Central Army launched a general offensive against Fujian, Military Special Envoy Du Qiyun arrived in Xiamen on the 2nd of this month and consulted with Lin Guogeng about recovering Xiamen. Chairman Chiang and the Naval Department also telegraphed, ordering the recovery to be implemented by the 5th of this month. At that time, Lin Guogeng believed that Xiamen was home to various foreign nationals, especially many Taiwanese residents of Japan. If there were military action, it would inevitably give foreigners an excuse. In fact, Japanese warships had already moved to the Narcissus Palace wharf on the 5th, with their gun covers removed. If there were battles in the city, Japanese sailors would certainly take the opportunity to land. Since the 4th, Taiwanese residents throughout the city had been flying the Japanese flag. Under these circumstances, Lin decided to resolve the issue through political means and secretly telegraphed the central government, requesting a postponement of the recovery. He also consulted with Huang Qiang about a peaceful recovery method. In fact, only three companies of the 19th Route Army were stationed in Xiamen, and there were no troops to transfer from Zhangzhou. Huang then agreed to telegraph Fuzhou for instructions. Later, he received a reply from Cai Tingkai, not allowing the transfer. On the 9th, Lin and Du received a telegram from the central government and the Naval Department, setting a deadline of the 10th to recover Xiamen. Lin again summoned Huang Qiang and informed him that the situation was such that resistance was futile. Huang agreed to withdraw. That evening at 7:00 PM, Huang crossed over to Gulangyu and ordered Mayor Luo Zongmeng to hand over the city government. Public Security Bureau Director Lin Hongfei also agreed to withdraw. Lin Guogeng then appointed Wang Zongshi, the director of the Third Branch Bureau, as the acting director of the Public Security Bureau to take over the Public Security Bureau. Huang Guanxi, the commander of the 1st Battalion of the Special Service Regiment of the 19th Route Army stationed in Xiamen, consisting of three infantry companies, one machine gun company, and one military police company, totaling over 700 men, was originally a former subordinate of Du Qiyun and had been contacted in advance to surrender. By the morning of the 10th, Du Qiyun sent Xie Jingbo, the commander of the Fujian Independent 1st Brigade, to inspect and reorganize Huang's unit and appointed Huang as the regimental commander. However, there was still a twist in the takeover of the Public Security Bureau. Lin Hongfei had originally agreed to hand it over and had Wang Zongshi escort him to Daomei, crossing the river to Gulangyu. Unexpectedly, Lin had a change of heart upon arriving in Gulangyu and telegraphed the bureau secretary Tan Yujun, refusing the takeover. Tan immediately notified each branch bureau by telephone not to hand over. All branch bureaus did not comply. Tan Yujun then ordered the special service team, security team, and military police team to take emergency precautions. The situation suddenly changed. Lin returned to Xiamen and received the report. He then telephoned Huang Qiang to discuss a peaceful solution. Huang said he could not stop it, and there was no result. Thus, from 11:00 PM on the 9th, the naval side began military deployments. Chen Wenlong, the captain of the security team stationed at the Dabei Pavilion in front of the park, was the first to break away from the Public Security Bureau and become independent. Feng Hongxiang, the captain of the security battalion stationed at Fuyu Cape, although a figure in the 19th Route Army, had many Northern and Fujian natives in his unit and had previously expressed sympathy for the navy. They also left their unit headquarters in groups of three or five and transferred to the Dabei Pavilion. Seeing that the situation was not right, Feng sneaked across to Gulangyu. At the same time, the Special Envoy's Office also deployed hundreds of plainclothes officers, distributed in the Public Security Bureau, Xiamen Port, Zhongshan Road, Haihou, Fuyu Cape, and other areas. At this time, the Naval Port Headquarters had ordered Wang Zongshi to act as the director of the Public Security Bureau, sending Special Service Team Captain Wang Chaoqu and Security 2nd Team Squad Leader Guo Zhongying to lead a platoon of security guards to cooperate with a company of marines to the Public Security Bureau. First, they disarmed the police guarding the door, and then disarmed the special service team, confiscating 31 Mauser pistols (8 missing), over 30 Qu-7 and Qu-9 pistols, 3 rifles, 3 revolvers, and some ammunition. Yang Yiming, the captain of the special service team, was detained. Then, they entered the bureau. Secretary Tan Yujun and former Heshan Police Chief Yu Lan were also in the bureau and were also detained. Lin Tianhong (Lin Hongzhu), the captain of the special service detective team, and Xu Zhao寰, director of the 5th Branch Bureau, were also detained. The overall situation was stabilized by about 6:00 AM on the 10th. At dawn, the Naval Port Headquarters posted a notice, which read: "Notice: This Headquarters has received a telegram from the Naval Department of the Central Government, setting a deadline to recover Xiamen as soon as possible, requiring the entire city to fly the Blue Sky White Sun flag, etc. Now, the 19th Route Army has completely left Xiamen. This headquarters is fully responsible for maintaining local security. Foreign residents should be given comprehensive and practical protection. This notice is hereby issued to all merchants and people of Xiamen for their information. This is a notice issued on January 10th, 23rd year of the Republic of China, by Commander Lin Guogeng." Military Special Envoy Du Qiyun also issued a notice, which read: "This Special Envoy is ordered to come to Fujian, responsible for suppressing the rebellion and pacifying the people. Commander Lin is responsible for maintaining security in Xiamen." Lin established the Special Envoy's Office in the former municipal government building on the same day. The department included a staff, adjutant, secretary, military law, accounting, and five sections, as well as a political department. At the same time, Du telegraphed the central government, requesting that Liu Guangqian be appointed as the mayor of Xiamen and the magistrate of Siming County. Liu will take over the city and county governments after the central government's order arrives. At noon, the Naval Port Headquarters appointed Han Fuhai as the director of the Xiamen Finance Bureau. Han immediately went to various tax collection agencies to take over. In addition, the agencies that have been taken over include the Tax Bureau, the Consolidated Tax Bureau, the Stamp Tax and Tobacco and Alcohol Tax Bureau, the Kerosene Special Tax Bureau, the Imported Rice Tax Bureau, the Official Property Clearance Bureau, the Sugar Industry Business Tax Bureau, and the Sulfur Business Tax Bureau. As for the Salt Transport Deputy Office and the Inspection Office, the previous incumbents had moved all items and documents to Gulangyu the night before. Regarding the courts, the Special Envoy's Office appointed Yang Tingshu to concurrently serve as the President of the First High Branch Court. Yang also went to take over and appointed Liu Liangqi to temporarily serve as the President of the Siming District Court. Zhao Bing, the original President of the High Branch Court, and Lin Chao, the President of the District Court, had both fled. The inspection system, which had been abolished by the pseudo-organization, has now been restored. Mi Anren, the Prosecutor of the High Court Inspection Office, and Chen Bin嶼, the local inspection officer, have taken office. Regarding party affairs, the Special Envoy's Office appointed Lu Duzhen, Chen Li, and Huang Xihuang as members of the Siming City Party Affairs Reorganization Committee and established a reorganization committee. They issued a notice to the Kuomintang members in the city, setting a deadline of the 18th of this month to report to the meeting for reorganization, and those who fail to report by the deadline will have their membership revoked. After Wang Zongshi took office as the Director of the Public Security Bureau, the personnel of each bureau were redistributed.

Torpedo Fleet Commander Wang Shouting, aboard the "Yi Xian" warship, and Lin Liang's unit, the 7th Company of the 3rd Battalion of the 2nd Regiment of the Marine Corps transported by the "Zhongshan" warship, arrived in Xiamen from Sandu'ao at 6:00 AM on the 10th. Lin's company landed and was stationed at the Pan Shi battery. After arriving in Xiamen, Wang also landed and visited Lin Guogeng and Du Qiyun to discuss defense. Wang came to assist Lin Guogeng in commanding the fleet for coordinated defense by order of the Naval Department. After returning to the warship, Wang ordered the "Jiangzhen" to sail to Gao'an, the "Yongjian" to sail to Wutong, the "Chuqian" to sail to Songyu, and the "Yi Xian" and "Zhongshan" to be stationed at Monkey Island. The command warship is the "Yi Xian." There are currently five warships stationed in Xiamen. It is also heard that the 3rd Battalion of the Marine Corps, including the 8th Company of Lin Jiyuan, the 9th Company of Zhu Fengxiang, and the machine gun company of Zhang Binqin, will be transported to Xiamen by the "Chu Guan" warship and the "Ding An" warship on the 11th. The 7th Company of the battalion was originally stationed at Xiangshan Port. The battalion headquarters and the 8th, 9th, and machine gun companies were all stationed in Nanjing. They left Nanjing and Xiangshan on the 4th and arrived at Sandu'ao on the night of the 9th. Before they could assemble, the 7th Company received an order from Chen Jiliang to rush to Xiamen at 9:00 PM. It is also said that Chen's regiment is currently engaged in fierce fighting with Qiu Zhaochen's unit in the Feiluan Ridge area of Luoyuan, and has not yet been able to depart for Xiamen immediately. It will probably have to wait another day or two.

Regarding foreigners, because Xiamen was recovered in one night and there was no local disorder, although there were those who were eager to cause trouble, there was no movement. Among Fujian's international relations, Xiamen is the most complex and difficult to deal with. Now that it has been able to pass so smoothly, the people of Xiamen are quite fortunate. (11th)

Hankou Cracks Down on Fujian Rebel Organization 110

Seized Seal of Pseudo-Commander-in-Chief

The Ring Leader Tang Nanqing Has Been Executed by Firing Squad

Hankou dispatch: Since the outbreak of the Fujian Incident, it has been rumored that the pseudo-organization sent party members to various places to engage in activities. The Pacification Commissioner's Office in Hubei and the Garrison Headquarters, considering Wuhan's strategic importance, repeatedly ordered their subordinates to strengthen precautions to avoid disrupting public order. Since January, many suspected reactionaries have been arrested, but most lack concrete evidence. Therefore, they were either granted bail or detained for interrogation. On the 11th of last month, the 5th Regiment of the Central Military Police stationed in Hankou cracked down on a reactionary organization in Yaobang Alley, Hankou. Five criminals were arrested at the time, and the seal of the pseudo-commander-in-chief of the 4th Route Army of the pseudo-Chinese People's Revolutionary Army, commission certificates, orders, rosters, and other items were seized. After being sent to the Garrison Department for interrogation and clarification, the ring leader Tang Nanqing was sentenced to death, and Ma Shaofu and the other four were sentenced to twelve years in prison. A telegram was sent to Chairman Chiang for approval. On the 11th of this month, an instruction from the Nanchang Headquarters was received approving the sentence. That afternoon at 6:00 PM, the Garrison Department executed the criminal Tang by firing squad and announced the charges. This is the first case of a reactionary criminal being executed after the Fujian Incident. The charges are recorded as follows: "Case investigation: On December 11 of last year, it was found that the 5th Regiment of the Central Military Police had sent a letter regarding the arrest of five reactionary criminals, Tang Nanqing, Xiong Meilin, Ma Shaofu, Zhao Fuchou, and Mi Fuqing, at No. 14 Yaobang Alley in Hankou, and the seal of the pseudo-commander-in-chief of the 4th Route Army of the pseudo-Chinese People's Revolutionary Army, commission certificates, orders, rosters, and other items seized, to the department. After being instructed to hand it over to the Military Law Office for separate review, it was confirmed that Tang Nanqing was a cadre of the pseudo-organization and harbored the pseudo-deputy commander Wang Hongjun, using the shared residence as a reactionary organ, and engaged in activities everywhere. Ma Shaofu and others were all introduced by him to join the organization. When the Fujian Incident occurred, Wuhan was filled with military police. Tang Nanqing dared to carry out reactionary activities and incite others to collude with traitors, which is unforgivable. In accordance with the provisions of Article 2, Paragraph 1, of the Emergency Law for Punishing Crimes Endangering the Republic of China, he should be sentenced to death. Ma Shaofu, Xiong Meilin, Zhao Fuchou, and Mi Fuqing are all guilty of inciting others to collude with traitors and should each be sentenced to twelve years in prison. The judgment has been drafted and submitted to Chairman Chiang's Nanchang Headquarters, Decree No. 230. In addition to Ma Shaofu and others who have been sentenced and sent to prison for execution, it is imperative to sign and bring Tang Nanqing, verify his identity, tie him to the execution ground for execution by firing squad, and announce it to all. This announcement is made by Tang Nanqing, 46 years old, from Hanyang County, Hubei." (11th)

Chairman Chiang Commends Song's Division for Recapturing Yanping 111

| Praising Its Glory as No Less Than the Huizhou Campaign |

Nanchang Dispatch: Chairman Chiang believes that in the Battle of Yanping this time, in the Battle of Jiufeng, the rebels had deep trenches and strong fortifications, and were determined to block and defend, but Song's division did not wait for the assistance of the air force and artillery, and went straight down in one go. The rebel army surrendered in the wind. Yesterday, he specially issued a commendation order. The original order read: "This time in the Battle of Yanping, it was all thanks to the brave and life-risking service of our army's generals and soldiers, and the effective command of Commander Liu, who were able to pacify the rebel atmosphere in one fell swoop and recapture the famous city. At the beginning of the battle, it was believed that the rebel army's fortifications on Jiufeng Mountain were strong and difficult to attack. Therefore, only a part of Song's division was ordered to perform a supporting attack on Jiufeng Mountain. The air force and artillery fully assisted our main force in the bombing of the northeast of Yanping, originally hoping to capture Yanping first, and then attack Jiufeng Mountain. However, Song's division did not wait for the assistance of the air force and artillery, and immediately used a part to fight against its mortar and attack independently. After a day of fierce and hard fighting on Jiufeng Mountain, although officers and soldiers were killed and wounded repeatedly, they were not afraid at all, and they advanced one after another. Finally, at Weiriwei, they broke through the rebel's strong fortifications on Jiufeng Mountain, and its position was completely occupied by our Song's division. As a result, the rebel army was terrified. In addition, due to the fierce attack of our main force Liu's division in the northeast of Yanping, they occupied the Mingcui Pavilion fortress, and various important places in the northeast. The rebels left the city and surrendered. The glory of the Battle of Yanping this time, and the loyalty and bravery of our generals and soldiers, are no less than the recapture of Huizhou in the fourteenth year. It is indeed a manifestation of the revolutionary spirit. The independent and fearless spirit of Division Commander Song, and the loyalty and bravery of his subordinates, are especially commendable. I hereby issue a commendation order, and I hope that all the generals and soldiers of our army will be inspired, work hard to suppress the rebellion, bravely strive to be the first, and complete the great cause of the revolution, to comfort our President Sun and the spirits of the fallen soldiers in heaven. This order is issued by Chiang Chung-cheng."

Another dispatch: The National Army attacked Shuikou on the morning of the 7th, and after a day of fierce fighting, they finally completely recovered it in the afternoon. The headquarters has now received a report that a large number of the main rebel force were captured in this battle, and more than 1,300 rifles, 11 machine guns, 8 mortars, and countless ammunition were seized. The remnants fled to the south bank of Shuikou and were all intercepted and resolved by a certain unit of the National Army. (January 10th)

North Ning Railway Joint Transport Train Derailment 112

Location: Between Fengtai and Changxindian

Cause: Old and Poorly Maintained Tracks

Two Cars Destroyed, Losses of 20,000 Yuan

Beijing Correspondence: Since the North Ning Railway started handling joint transport of goods, monthly revenue has increased sharply. Unexpectedly, at 2:50 AM on the 10th, a joint transport train derailed near kilometer marker 18 between Fengtai and Changxindian. The locomotive of the train was North Ning locomotive number 228, pulling 20 freight cars. A total of four freight cars were damaged. It is reported that when the locomotive reached a poor section of the track, the force of the wheels broke the rails. The first car did not leave the tracks, but nine cars, from the second to the tenth, derailed. Among them, the fourth, fifth, sixth, and seventh cars rolled down the embankment, which was about eight feet deep. Two freight cars were completely crushed, and the remaining two had partial damage. As for the tenth to twentieth freight cars, they were unharmed. After the accident, Zhang Pan, the deputy section chief of the North Ning Railway's locomotive department, urgently telegraphed the Fengtai car service and locomotive departments, as well as the locomotive department of the railway bureau, to report the derailment. The North Ning Railway immediately dispatched engineer Gu from the engineering department, section chief Li Xuxun from the locomotive department, and section chief Xiao Shufang from the car service department, along with deputy section chief Pan, to conduct a detailed investigation. After obtaining the results, they plan to prepare a report and submit it to the railway bureau. Traffic was restored at 1:20 AM on the 11th. According to staff from the joint transport department, the derailment was caused by the rails near kilometer marker 18 being too old and poorly maintained. These rails were manufactured by the Hanyang Arsenal in 1898 and are now over 30 years old. After investigation, it was proven that the rails were too weak, which led to the unfortunate derailment. The losses were significant, including 190 damaged railroad ties, 5 damaged rails, and severe damage to the cars. Total losses exceeded 20,000 yuan, and the delay in traffic was 24 hours, resulting in substantial business losses. Because most of the cars were freight cars, there were few deaths. The four cars that rolled down the embankment will be loaded later due to the time required for unloading. The other five cars were rerouted by the Ping Han locomotive department, and the roadbed and rails were repaired by the Ping Han Railway engineering department. (11th)

Jiangyin

Education Department Approves Reorganization of County Education 114

After the Provincial Department of Education sent provincial supervisor Feng Ce and others to Cheng to conduct a special inspection for the reorganization of county education, the reorganization plan has been submitted to the department for approval. Currently, the following has been determined: The county-run normal school will be wound down this semester, and the existing class of students will be managed by the provincial Louxiashan Rural Normal School. All school equipment will be received by the Education Bureau. Schools in various districts will be consolidated due to the accumulation of unpaid educational expenses. For example, Shoushan Primary School in Yu District will be merged with the central primary school, and Tanxiang Primary School will be merged with Chengbei Primary School. Zhouzhuang North Street Primary School, Yanshan Primary School, Daizhuang Primary School, Qingtang Primary School, and Caizhuang Primary School, Xujing Primary school are all slated for closure. Other schools, such as Ma Zhen Guanshan Township Primary School, have also been closed in large numbers. Grades five and six of Qiaoqi Primary School and Yueqiao Primary School will be combined into one grade. Beiwai Juyong and Beidajie Primary Schools will be privatized. The middle street Louxia Elementary School will be transformed into a private school. Teacher salary standards will be divided into three levels, in accordance with Wuxi: Level 1, high school normal school graduates, monthly salary of 30 to 40 yuan; Level 2, high school graduates, monthly salary of 20 to 30 yuan; Level 3, county normal school graduates, monthly salary of 16 to 20 yuan. This will take effect on February 1. Education Bureau expenses will also be greatly reduced. County supervisor Chen Changyan is being removed. Provincial supervisors will come to Cheng within a few days to carry out the reorganization.

Zhu Baoyuan's Widow Sues Two Sons for Division of Property 121

Another Hearing Was Held Yesterday

Both Sides Hold to Their Own Views

After the death of Zhu Baoyuan, owner of Zhenhe Tea Shop, his widow Zhu Xixinbao sued Baoyuan's two sons, Zhu Yanqing and Zhu Shunqing, for failing to distribute 630,000 yuan of inheritance. She hired lawyer Chen Ying to file a lawsuit with the First Special District District Court for division of property. The two defendants also hired lawyer Zhang Zhengxue to defend them, arguing that Baoyuan's estate was only over 680,000 yuan, and after deducting 80,000 yuan for ancestral sacrifices, only a little over 600,000 yuan was available for distribution, with each person receiving 100,000 yuan. The District Court has repeatedly summoned all parties for questioning, as reported in previous newspapers. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Qiao Wanxuan held another hearing. According to the plaintiff Zhu Xixinbao, Baoyuan had a property ledger during his lifetime, which he wrote himself. The ledger was always placed on the table in the bedroom, and I saw it, but I do not know the specific items and amounts of property. Therefore, I request that an accountant be appointed to audit the accounts, and the distribution should be based on what is found in the future. After Baoyuan died, the bedroom was sealed. After more than ten days, the door was reopened, and all the furniture in the room was moved out. The two defendants then prepared new furniture for me, and the property ledger and other account books were packed and moved out by the defendants at that time, and so on. She also presented a bill, saying that this bill was given to me by Shunqing in Zhenhe Tea Shop, but the property listed in it does not seem to be complete. Defendant's lawyer Zhang Zhengxue immediately said that Baoyuan never had the so-called property ledger as claimed by the plaintiff. Although the plaintiff has repeatedly claimed that there is such a ledger and that the defendants took it away, she cannot prove it conclusively. The defendants only have a diary of their father, which details the types and amounts of property, as well as the business situation of Zhenhe and the contact information of relatives and friends. He then showed this diary to the plaintiff, asking if it was Baoyuan's belongings and if it was his handwriting. After the plaintiff looked at it, she said that the diary was indeed his belongings, and the larger characters written in the book were also Baoyuan's handwriting, but the smaller characters seemed difficult to identify and did not look like his writing. Lawyer Zhang then stated to the court that the plaintiff was making insincere statements. This diary was written by Baoyuan himself, but she said it did not look like his handwriting. The plaintiff must have many handwritten notes by Baoyuan in her collection. Please order her to produce them for verification, which should clarify the matter. The plaintiff then said that I have no scraps of paper or words from Baoyuan's hand, as they were completely taken away when the furniture was moved. The plaintiff's lawyer then requested: 1) to obtain Baoyuan's handwritten property ledger; 2) the full Zhenhe business accounts for the past five years; 3) to summon additional witnesses. Lawyer Zhang then said that in addition to the handwritten diary of Baoyuan that has now been submitted, there is no so-called property ledger. Furthermore, the plaintiff's lawsuit is for division of property, not for auditing accounts. Zhenhe's business and Baoyuan's estate are two completely separate matters and cannot be discussed together. However, in order to dispel the plaintiff's suspicions, the defendants have voluntarily sent Zhenhe's account books to an accountant for verification. Now that the court wants to review them, it should notify the parties concerned to comply. Judge Qiao then questioned the witnesses who were present about the financial dealings they had with Zhu Baoyuan, and then adjourned the hearing to a later date.

Yin Xianfu Convicted of Embezzling Funds from Kangyuan Factory 122

After the Detective Office Appealed to the Supreme Court

The Case Was Returned for Retrial and He Was Sentenced to Six Months Imprisonment

Xiang Kangyuan, the owner of Kangyuan Printing and Can Manufacturing Factory, in the spring of 1930, commissioned Yin Xianfu, a native of Suzhou, to handle the registration of the factory's branch in Singapore and remitted 1,500 yuan from the Shanghai headquarters to cover all expenses. However, Yin secretly pocketed the money and falsely claimed that the money had been given to a local lawyer and agent Zheng Tianfu to entrust to lawyer Xue Feike Dansi for handling. He also forged Xue's English receipt and sent it back to the headquarters to cover up the matter. Later, he used the excuse of fostering relationships with Singaporean gentry and businessmen to promote business and embezzled 300 yuan from the factory, reporting that it was a commission paid to Hu Wentao's nephew Hu Guigeng for promoting products. However, Xiang Kangyuan later discovered that everything was fabricated. After Yin returned to Shanghai, Xiang reported the matter to the Detective Office, which sent detectives to arrest Yin. After completing the investigation, they filed a lawsuit with the First Special District District Court for embezzlement. The initial trial resulted in a verdict of not guilty, as the defendant was found to have no embezzling act. The Detective Office, believing that the evidence was sufficient, appealed the original verdict to the Second Branch of the Jiangsu High Court. However, the second instance still resulted in a verdict of not guilty. The Detective Office then filed a third appeal with the Supreme Court. Lawyer Ru Baoyi pointed out the improprieties of the initial two trials and presented his reasons for disagreeing with the verdicts. The petition was very lengthy. After reviewing the entire record, the Supreme Court found that the original verdict was too lenient and that the acquittal was insufficient to convince. The Supreme Court vacated the original verdict and remanded the case to the Second Branch of the High Court for retrial. The High Court then sent all written evidence, such as the lawyer's receipt and related correspondence, to the Zhenru Forensic Institute for authentication. The institute's report proved that the receipts and letters were forged. It also sent a letter to the Chinese Consulate in Singapore to inquire whether there was a lawyer named Xue in Singapore and whether Zheng Tianfu existed, which Yin could not confirm. Hu Guigeng was also summoned to court, and Hu solemnly stated that he had never received any commission. The letter he sent to Yin Xianfu originally contained the words "蒙賜數物 (received several items)," but Yin presented a photograph of the letter with the words changed to "蒙賜三數 (received three numbers)." If he had presented the original letter, the flaws would have been easily exposed. The presiding judge of the criminal court, Yu Hua, and judges Zhao Zhengzhang and Lin Wopeng, having concluded their investigation of all evidence and witnesses, were clear about the situation. They then scheduled an oral argument. Lawyer Ru Baoyi of the Detective Office argued that the case had been investigated several times, and this investigation was particularly detailed. The defendant's forgery of receipts and alteration of letters had been strongly proven. Therefore, it would be difficult for him to escape responsibility for the crime of continuous embezzlement of property in the course of business. He requested that the previous improper verdicts be overturned and that the defendant be punished according to the law. Yin also hired lawyers Zhang Feixiong and Zhang Shibeng to defend him. The verdict has now been announced. The main text is that the original verdict is vacated, and Yin Xianfu is sentenced to six months imprisonment for continuous embezzlement of items held in the course of business. The number of days of detention before the verdict is determined will be counted as one day of imprisonment for every two days.

Recent Property and Land Taxes Implemented by the French Concession 129

The Shanghai French Concession Council recently reported the land tax, property tax, and other taxes to be implemented starting in 1934, as follows: 1) Land Tax: For all properties located within the French Concession, in addition to the provisions of Article 6 of the agreement of April 8, 1914, all tax rates should be levied at 80% of 1% of the land value. This land tax should be paid every six months. 2) Property Tax: "Type 1" The tax rate for Type 1 is set at 13% of the total rent, payable quarterly by the tenant. The resolution of this board of directors on December 30, 1930, regarding the method of collecting taxes on leased houses, should still be implemented in 1934. Regarding property tax for owner-occupied houses, the rental value of the house should be estimated according to the following method, and 13% of the value should be taxed: "Section 1" The rental value from the French Bund to the east of Min Ti Ni Yin Road, extending to Lan Wei Ai Road, is estimated as follows: Houses and vacant land should be calculated at 5% of the total estimated value of the property. "Section 2" The rental value from the west of Min Ti Ni Yin Road and Lan Wei Ai Road to the east of Lu Ban Road, extending to Bai Liang Bu Road, is estimated as follows: Houses should be calculated at 6% of the total estimated value of the property. Vacant land: 1) Under three mu, should be calculated at 6% of the total estimated value of the property; 2) Three mu to six mu, calculated at 4%; 3) Six mu to nine mu, calculated at 2%; 4) Over nine mu, calculated at 1%. "Section 3" The rental value from the west of Lu Ban Road and Bai Er Bu Road to the east of Ya Er Bei Road is estimated as follows: Houses should be calculated at 7% of the total estimated value of the property. Vacant land: 1) Under three mu, should be calculated at 7% of the total estimated value of the property; 2) Three mu to six mu, calculated at 4%; 3) Six mu to nine mu, calculated at 2%; 4) Over nine mu, calculated at 1%. "Section 4" The rental value in the 1914 extension of Ya Er Bei Road to the west is estimated as follows: Houses should be calculated at 8% of the total estimated value of the property. Vacant land: 1) Under three mu, should be calculated at 8% of the total estimated value of the property; 2) Three mu to six mu, calculated at 4%; 3) Six mu to nine mu, calculated at 2%; 4) Over nine mu, calculated at 1%. The above-mentioned method of reducing the estimated rental value cannot be applied to the property tax on houses and vacant land used for commercial or industrial purposes. Regarding the property tax on sublet buildings, it should be calculated proportionally based on the benefit enjoyed by the tenant and the total rent, as follows: 1) Sublet buildings with heating equipment should be calculated at 90% of their rental value; 2) Sublet buildings with heating and running water equipment should be calculated at 85% of their rental value; 3) Sublet buildings with heating and lighting equipment should be calculated at 85% of their rental value; 4) Sublet buildings with heating, lighting, and running water equipment should be calculated at 80% of their rental value. In addition to heating, lighting, and running water equipment, sublet buildings with other comfortable facilities, such as elevators, air conditioning, swimming pools, private parlors, indoor tennis courts, and garbage incinerators, should be calculated at 70% of their rental value. However, the amount of property tax on sublet buildings may be agreed upon by special agreement based on the rental value of the house. This basis should be revised every two years. Property Tax "Type 2" The tax rate for Type 2 is set at 13% of the total rent, payable every two months by the tenant. The above-mentioned provisions regarding the method of collecting taxes on leased houses, owner-occupied houses, and sublet buildings are applicable to this Type 2 property tax. The method of collecting taxes on leased houses by this board of directors on December 30, 1930, should still be implemented in 1934.

Verification of a Modern Woman's Suicide on the Shanghai-Woosung Railway 130

The day before yesterday, a fashionable modern woman lay down on the Shanghai-Woosung Railway tracks in front of the Law School on Jiangwan Road, Zhabei, and committed suicide. Yesterday morning, Wang Jinfu, a local security officer from the Jiuyi map area, reported the incident to the District Court for verification. The court dispatched Inspector Ouyang to the scene to examine the body. The deceased was wearing an empty green woolen coat, a black wool camel hair cheongsam, a wrinkled silk short shirt and pants, high-heeled leather shoes, and flesh-colored stockings. She had been run over at the waist, and her right hand was also severed. As there were no family members present at the time, a charitable organization collected the body, awaiting investigation and notification of the family for claiming it. The official interrogated the local security officer that evening, who stated that after the incident, the investigating police and train driver stated that the deceased arrived in a car at 3:00 PM on the 11th of this month, asking for the railway to Jiangwan. At 3:09 PM, the Woosung train arrived from Shanghai, and the woman immediately laid down, resulting in her being crushed to death. The railway police found five yuan in banknotes, three yuan in silver dollars, and six jiao in small coins near the deceased's body, all of which are at the police station. The official instructed to investigate and handle the matter.

The Shanghai South Temporary Shelter Reports on Operational Status 136

Mr. Zhang Zixin, the General Manager of the Shanghai South Temporary Shelter, submitted a document yesterday to Mr. Wang Yiting and Mr. Huang Hanzhi, the two chairmen of the Shanghai Charity Organization Federation, stating: "Respectfully submitted, since the establishment of our shelter on the 24th of last month, we have set up three branch shelters. As of yesterday, we have registered and sheltered a total of 2,179 civilians. Among them, 297 people have voluntarily left the shelter or have been claimed by their families, 39 people have been sent to the hospital for treatment, and 12 people have died. Currently, there are 633 people living in the first shelter at the South Railway Station, the Huzhou Guildhall, 824 people living in the second shelter at the Huhui Villa on Xietu Road, and 374 people living in the third shelter at the Great King Temple on Great King Temple Street. The three shelters have a total of 1,831 residents. We need more than thirteen dan of rice per day, averaging seven he of rice per person. However, the shelter is severely lacking in cotton clothing. Recently, the weather has turned cold suddenly, and the civilians are suffering from hunger and cold. They are flocking to the shelter in droves, which is pitiful. Therefore, we respectfully submit this request, hoping that your association will negotiate with various charitable organizations regarding the cotton clothing. Please raise as much as possible and allocate as much as possible, so that the civilians in the shelter will not suffer from lack of clothing. As for the operating expenses, we will strive to be thrifty in order to live up to your kindness. We also ask your association to send personnel to visit the shelters at any time to inspect and provide guidance. We are deeply grateful." Nightly Ghostly Howls Scare Away Apprentice, Thief Swaps Bed to Steal Vault Funds 139

Yao Lizheng vehemently denied it and narrowly escaped

Ultimately unable to escape the law, he was sentenced to more than a year in prison

Yao Lizheng, 28 years old from Zhenjiang, used to work at a rubber factory in Shanghai but was dismissed for misconduct and became unemployed. He temporarily resided at the Yikang Money Shop on Avenue Edward VII, No. 68, managed by Huang Zibin, a fellow townsman. Every night, Yao slept in the main hall. Yao saw that the vault in the main hall contained a large number of banknotes and had malicious intentions. However, because an apprentice slept in the vault every night as a guard, he could not get started. In December of last year, after everyone had gone to bed, he pretended to be a ghost howling and used other supernatural powers to scare away the apprentice. The young apprentice was timid and was indeed frightened away. He swapped beds with Yao, allowing Yao to calmly open the vault and steal 7,600 yuan in cash, which he sent to his mistress Yu Xiuying at No. 538 Yongxing Road, Zhabei. After the shop discovered this, they reported it to the police, who sent detectives to investigate. Yao vehemently denied it. The detective suspected foul play but had no choice but to conduct a secret investigation. However, Yao was the prime suspect, so they sent someone to secretly follow and investigate him. Yao, thinking he had narrowly escaped, spent a lot of money, buying coats, fur coats, and cameras, and paying off debts. He also took his mistress to Suzhou for a trip. The detective found out and arrested Yao. After interrogation, he confessed and led them to recover 6,200 yuan in stolen money from his mistress's house. Both Yao Lizheng and his mistress Yu Xiuying were arrested and handed over to the Second Special District Court for prosecution. The details have been reported in previous newspapers. The trial has concluded, and yesterday Sun Pengxian, a judge of the Eighth Criminal Court, sentenced Yao Lizheng to one year and six months in prison for theft, and Yu Xiuying to two months in prison for receiving stolen goods. The stolen goods were returned to the owner.

Pretending to be a Son to Defraud Money 140

Once is already too much, how can it happen again?

Continuous Fraud Resulted in a Six-Month Sentence

Wang Zhendong from Guangdong used to be in the tin mining business in Nanyang and accumulated considerable wealth. His son, Wang Fupeng, studied at Zhijiang University in Hangzhou. However, there was a fellow townsman named Zhang Youwu, 27 years old, who claimed to have served in the Volunteer Army outside the customs. After retiring, he became destitute in Shanghai, staying in a cheap hotel and unable to find work, which led to financial difficulties. In December of last year, he used Wang Fupeng's name to send a telegram to Wang Zhendong in Nanyang, saying that he was ill and stranded in Room 102 of the Far East Hotel on Xizang Road, Shanghai. He had no money for medicine and urgently requested that several hundred yuan be remitted to Shanghai to relieve his immediate need. After receiving the telegram, Wang Zhendong believed it to be true and immediately remitted 250 yuan. Zhang obtained the large sum of money and squandered it at will. In just a few days, his pockets were empty again. However, he recalled that the previous method could still be used. On the 10th of this month, he sent another telegram to Wang Zhendong, saying that the previous sum had been received, but his illness was severe and he had not recovered. The money was gone, and he requested that another 300 yuan be remitted to Room 318 of the Asia Hotel on Avenue Edward VII in the French Concession. After receiving this telegram, Wang Zhendong became suspicious. His son was studying in Hangzhou, how could he suddenly fall ill in Shanghai? He also sent a telegram to his nephew Wang Bo, asking him to investigate nearby. Wang Bo was studying at the Dongwu Law School on Kunshan Road. After receiving his uncle's telegram, he knew that Wang Fuyue was studying at Zhijiang University in Hangzhou and was in good health. He had just received a letter from him a few days ago, so how could he suddenly be sick in Shanghai? Something was clearly wrong. He remained calm and went to the Asia Hotel yesterday morning to investigate. He saw the name Wang Fu written in the registration book for Room 318 and saw that the room door was closed. He went to the French Concession Police Station to report. The head detective said that the incident occurred in the Public Concession and instructed him to report to the English Concession. Wang Bo then went to the Lao Zha Police Station and stated the previous situation. Detective Xie Guisheng went to Room 318 of the Asia Hotel and arrested Zhang Shiwu, confiscating two telegram receipts. He was taken to the police station for detention. Yesterday morning, he was sent to the Second Criminal Court of the First Special District. Qian Xunjiu, the police lawyer, detailed the above situation, saying that the police were prosecuting him for fraud under Article 363 of the Criminal Code and requested that he be punished according to law. Wang Bo also submitted a statement of the investigation. When questioned, the defendant Zhang Shiwu confessed to the charges and asked for leniency. Judge Wu Xiangzu verified the confession and sentenced Zhang Shiwu to three months of imprisonment for continuous fraud.

To Avoid the Stigma of "Sick Man of East Asia," Everyone Must Ascend to Longevity City

Reception for the Press 142

Speech and Notes 143

However, the tuberculosis death rate in our country is as high as 307 people. This is six times the death rate of New Zealand, four times that of Egypt and the United States, three and a half times that of Germany, three times that of the United Kingdom, two and a half times that of Spain, and one and a half times that of France and Japan." However, this number should not be regarded as the tuberculosis death rate in China, because the climate of Beiping is the most suitable climate in the country for health. With the superior climate of Beiping, there are still 307 people out of every 100,000 who are captured by the tuberculosis army. Then, the increase in the number of people whose climate south of the Yangtze River is not suitable for the health of the nation should not be surprising. If we do not seek to cope with it as soon as possible, then the consequences will be unimaginable. The methods are: (1) implement remedial treatment for those who are already ill; (2) implement tuberculosis prevention for those who are not yet ill." Ministry of Communications Prohibits Three Seagoing Vessels from Sailing 144

Shun Yuan, Yu Da, and Yu Tong Three Ships

All Foreign Crew Members Have No Ministry Certification

Ministry Order Arrived in Shanghai After Ships Had Already Sailed

The Ministry of Communications has expressly ordered that shipowners of Chinese merchant ships who employ foreign crew members who have not undergone inspection or applied for a supplementary examination and certificate renewal are not allowed to continue employing them. Violators will have their ships seized and prohibited from sailing. This time, the Yu Da Company's Yu Da and Yu Tong, and the Yongyuan Company's Shun Yuan have shipmasters, chief mates, and chief engineers who are all foreign nationals, who have not been inspected by the Ministry of Communications and have deliberately violated the ministry's orders by not applying for a supplementary examination and certificate renewal, and are still working on the ships. This time, the three ships sailed from North China to Shanghai at the same time. After arriving in Shanghai, the issue of crew qualifications arose.

Yantai Maritime Bureau Obstructs 145

When the three ships came to Shanghai, they knew that none of the senior crew members were qualified for inspection, and according to regulations, they could not pass through Shanghai. When the ships sailed from Yantai, they requested the Yantai Maritime Bureau to send a telegram to Shanghai to lobby the Shanghai Maritime Bureau, requesting that the three ships be allowed to sail as usual. The Shanghai Maritime Bureau received the telegram and allowed Shun Yuan, Yu Da, and Yu Tong to pass through.

Master Mariners' Association Sends Telegram to the Ministry 146

After the Shun Yuan and other three ships entered the port, the Shanghai Merchant Mariners' Association learned that all the crew members were foreigners, none of them had certificates, and none of them had been inspected by the Ministry of Communications. This violated Article 16 of the Ministry's regulations for crew members, which stipulates that foreign crew members should not be allowed to work on Chinese ships. The association, based on the request of its members, sent an urgent telegram to the Ministry of Communications on the 9th of this month, requesting the Ministry to implement the suspension of the foreign crew members of the Shun Yuan, Yu Da, and Yu Tong, and to replace them with certified crew members who have passed the inspection, and to order the Shanghai Maritime Bureau to prohibit the ships from clearing customs and sailing.

Ministry Order Prohibits Sailing of Three Ships 147

The Master Mariners' Association feared that there would be a delay, so it sent an urgent telegram to the Ministry of Communications. At the same time, it submitted a copy of the telegram to the local Maritime Bureau, requesting that the three ships not be allowed to clear customs and sail. However, the day after the telegram was sent, there was no reply from the Ministry. It was not until the 11th that the Ministry's approval was received, stating that the request to ban the foreign crew members of the Shun Yuan, Yu Da, and Yu Tong from being inspected and to prohibit them from clearing customs should be followed. The order had been sent to the Maritime Bureau for compliance. Unfortunately, the Ministry's order prohibiting sailing arrived in Shanghai after the three ships had already cleared customs and left Shanghai a day earlier. Although they narrowly escaped this time, they may not be able to sail to Shanghai next time unless they replace the crew members with certified crew members.

Opinions of the Two Egg Industry Associations on Coping with Increased Taxes in Various Countries 148

Yesterday a letter was sent to the Trade Bureau to be forwarded to the Ministry of Industry and Commerce

Protesting to Various Countries to Reduce Import Tax Rates

Our country's egg exports have always occupied an important position. Taking exports to France as an example, it requires 20,000 to 30,000 dan per year. Last winter, the country restricted the quantity of our exports to more than 9,000 dan per year, which is a significant difference from the previous export volume. Then, it increased the import license tax on ice-cured eggs to 4.60 francs per net kilogram (French currency), which is almost a 100% tax rate, more than twice the tax on fresh eggs. Therefore, it has a huge impact on our country's egg exports. The local International Trade Bureau previously received an order from the Ministry of Industry and Commerce and held discussions with egg merchants on December 29 last year to discuss remedial measures. Now, the bureau has received opinions from the Shanghai Egg Industry Association and the Ice Egg Industry Association, requesting that they be forwarded to the Ministry of Industry and Commerce for approval. The original text is as follows:

Ice Egg Industry Association 149

The Ice Egg Industry Association sent a letter to the International Trade Bureau yesterday, stating, "We are writing to you because we have received a notice from your bureau that the French government intends to reserve three-quarters of all licenses for ice egg imports and exchange them conditionally at any time. This matter has a great impact on our country's ice egg exports to France. We held a meeting of ice egg exporters in this city on December 29 last year to discuss the situation, which has been recorded by your bureau. Since 1932, the French government has not only increased the original tax from 2% to 4%, but also added an import license tax of 400 francs per 100 kilograms last year, which is equivalent to about 50% of the ad valorem tax. Since the tax was levied, our ice egg exports to France have suffered a great blow. Now, it is intensifying the situation by restricting the issuance of licenses, which is close to monopolizing commerce and resisting the import of our country's native products. This is not appropriate in terms of commercial ethics. This is the first point. Moreover, ice eggs are food and cannot be compared to luxury goods. The French increase in the license tax is similar to a luxury tax. Now, it has increased the tax and added restrictions, and the restrictions are extremely harsh. Most of the French goods imported into our country are luxury goods and consumables. Our customs not only do not impose harsh taxes, but also do not impose restrictions. In terms of the principle of reciprocity in trade, the French government should not do this. This is the second point. Please check whether the French goods imported into China are more or less than our goods exported. If more French goods are imported into China, then our country is promoting so many luxury goods for France, and France should provide convenience for our country's egg imports. Now, it is not considering this, but restricting our ice egg imports. In terms of friendship, it is not appropriate to do this. This is the third point. According to our association's humble opinion, the countermeasures are divided into the following three steps: (1) Please ask the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to protest to the French government based on the above reasons and cancel the original proposal to retain three-quarters of the ice egg licenses, and return all ice egg import licenses to our country as usual. (2) If the protest is invalid, please ask the Ministry of Finance to handle French goods imported into our country in the same way as the country taxes our ice eggs, that is, increase the import tax rate and issue a license tax, and give one-quarter of the license to other countries that treat us equally. (3) If, after investigation, it is found that fewer French goods are imported into China than our goods are exported to France, then we should persuade them to realize the situation out of friendship. The relationship between China and France has always been strong, and commercial cooperation should be on the path of mutual prosperity. We should not have narrow views, restrict our imports, and lose our goodwill. Please ask the French government to return the three-quarters of the ice egg import license tax that has been retained to our country as usual. We have contributed these humble opinions, and we hope that your bureau will participate in the discussion and forward them to the Ministry of Industry and Commerce for prompt review and handling. We are truly grateful for your assistance."

Fresh Egg Industry Association 150

The Fresh Egg Industry Association sent a letter to the Trade Bureau, stating, "We are writing to you because we have recently found that various countries have repeatedly increased tariffs on our egg imports, especially Japan, the United States, Germany, France, Italy, and the Philippines. This has led to a decrease in our country's egg exports. At a time when rural areas are bankrupt, the export of local goods is a matter of life and death for rural areas. This must be remedied. We have considered that all countries in the East and West have surplus agricultural and industrial products, and our country is the final destination for sales. Our country's money exports must be tens of thousands of yuan. It can be seen that our assistance to the farmers and workers of various countries is not weak, and the benefits that various countries have received from us are not small. While we are doing our best to promote their surplus goods, they are restricting our imports, which violates the principle of trade and loses the balance of affairs. In May of last year, we submitted a report to Minister Song, proposing this opinion at the London Economic Conference, requesting a reduction in the import tax rate on eggs. Unexpectedly, the discussion was fruitless and became a pending case. However, our country's egg industry has been forced into a critical autumn. If we do not remedy it, we will follow the path of silk and tea and perish together. The impact on rural areas is huge. Therefore, we earnestly request that your bureau discuss a complete plan and effectively remedy the egg industry. We are extremely grateful. We offer two opinions: (1) We should ask the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to protest separately to various countries, requesting a reduction in the import tax rate on eggs. If this is ineffective, we should ask the Ministry of Finance to increase the import tax on imported goods from those countries in retaliation. (2) We should ask the Ministry of Finance to follow the common practice of various countries and exempt export egg taxes. All countries' increase in egg taxes and the resistance methods that our country should adopt are attached in detail for reference. We are extremely grateful for your assistance."

Those attending included Lu Jianquan, Director of the Central Mint, Wei Jingzhou, Deputy Director, Wei Tingtao, Director of the General Affairs Department, Qiao Furen, Secretary, and Ge Laide, Director of the Chemical Examination Office, totaling twenty-eight people.

Secretary's Report 153

By Chairman Kong Xiangxi, Li Zhezhang, and Feng Yanzhang, Recording. First, the chairman reported the purpose of the meeting, followed by Secretary Qiao Furen's report: ㈠ This council audited legal new currency of 4.75 million yuan in December, and supervised the stamping of Grade A ingot bars (999 fineness) of 1,133 bars and Grade B ingot bars (880 fineness) of 227 bars. In addition to approving the respective factory releases and posting public notices, we also sent a letter to the Ministry of Finance for record, requesting its inclusion in the "Finance Daily." ㈡ Committee member Jian Dongpu previously sent a letter to the council resigning his position. We immediately forwarded the letter to the Ministry of Finance based on the circumstances and reported it at the eighth regular meeting. Now, we have received a reply from the Ministry of Finance stating that the Ministry has directly informed Committee member Jian, approving his resignation. ㈢ Regarding the issuance date of the two types of ingot bars, the Ministry of Finance approved in a letter of December 25, setting January 1, 1934, as the issuance date for the two types of ingot bars, and clearly stipulated that Grade B ingot bars are only for the use of silver and money businesses for collection and settlement, and are not allowed to circulate outside, in order to show restrictions. ㈣ The council's October report to the Ministry was approved in a reply letter of December 14 and filed for record. ㈤ Regarding the casting of new currency and ingot bars, the factory cast new currency for 18 days in November, totaling 3,279,708 yuan, with an average daily output of 182,26 yuan. The amount transferred to the Central Bank was 3,200,000 yuan, which is consistent with the number approved by the council. In addition, in November, 923 Grade A 999 ingot bars were cast. 951 bars have been stamped by the council (including 28 bars from October stamped in November), and 900 bars were transferred to the Central Bank. ㈥ Regarding the name of the silver used and the amount of copper mixed, the silver ingots sent by the factory to the council daily for melting reports totaled 17, with a total weight of 8,194,862.76 ounces in November. This includes copper and mixed copper totaling 986,917.72 ounces. As a percentage, the silver content accounts for 87.96%, and the copper content accounts for 13.04%.

Chemical Analysis Report 154

Ge Lai, Director of the Chemical Analysis Office, reported that the Central Mint cast new currency totaling 4,750,000 yuan in December, which was sent to the council for review. We extracted 525 yuan in accordance with regulations for separate chemical analysis. The average fineness was 880.46, which is 0.46 higher than the statutory standard. The weight was 26.696 grams, which is approximately four ten-thousandths lower than the statutory raw weight, all within the statutory tolerance. Also, the 1,133 Grade A ingot bars with 999 fineness and the 227 Grade B ingot bars with 880 fineness, which passed the review in the same month, were also supervised and stamped by the chemical analysis师 during the comparison marking in accordance with regulations.

Total Cast Amount 155

The total amount of new currency and ingot bars cast by the Central Mint up to December of the 22nd year of the Republic of China: ㈠ Silver coins: 25,410,000 yuan with the new die, and 2,600,000 yuan with the old die. ㈡ Ingot bars: 3,550 Grade A bars and 200 Grade B bars. Furthermore, a reporter from the New Sound News Agency interviewed Secretary Qiao of the Review Committee yesterday, who stated that the two types of ingot bars were issued by the Central Bank on New Year's Day. The ingot bars cast by the Central Mint this month will be tested by the Review Committee and sent to the Central Bank for issuance at any time.

Shanghai and Hankou Commodity Inspection Bureaus Held Tea Improvement Meeting Yesterday 156

This Year's Export Standards Have Been Decided

Improvement Field Will Hold a Meeting Today to Discuss Implementation

Regarding the inspection of Chinese tea exports, strict standards are set every year to improve quality, increase international trade, prevent adulteration, and maintain overseas reputation. The implementation has been very effective. This year, the Shanghai and Hankou Commodity Inspection Bureaus are paying more attention to promoting quality. In order to crack down on colored tea and strictly limit moisture and ash content, it is necessary to revise the standards. Therefore, yesterday at 1 p.m., the 23rd Annual Standard Tea Revision Meeting was held in the Tea Inspection Room of the bureau. Attendees included Ye Yuanding, Fang Hanzhou, Wu Juenong, Hu Haochuan, and Zhou Zhenjun. Ye Yuanding was the chairman, Hu Haochuan was the recorder, and the formalities were observed. (A) Chairman's Report (omitted). (B) Matters for discussion: ㈠ How to revise the tea standard? Resolved: The red tea standard was passed according to the sample proposed by the Hankou Bureau. The green tea standard followed the 22nd annual standard. ㈡ How to revise the tea moisture content? Resolved: The moisture content of red and green tea should be 8.5%. However, this year, in addition to the standard for green tea, the moisture content of red tea should be 10.5% to pass, and the moisture content of other teas should be 12% to pass. ㈢ How to revise the tea ash content? Resolved: The maximum ash content of red and green tea should be 7%. ㈣ How to revise the color of colored tea? Resolved: Passed according to the sample proposed by the Shanghai Bureau. ㈤ How to decide on measures to crack down on colored tea? Resolved: ㈠ Merchants who declare colored tea for inspection must fill in the names of the coloring materials in detail. If necessary, they must submit all the coloring materials for inspection. ㈡ Tea that is excessively colored and the same or heavier than the established colored tea standard is prohibited from export. ㈢ The use of toxic coloring materials containing metals such as lead, copper, antimony, chromium, barium, and cadmium (such as the commonly used light yellow "Three Fish Yellow," "Yi Ji Huang," and "Sand Green") and other inorganic or organic substances is prohibited from export. ㈥ How to implement the motions of this session? Resolved: The two bureaus will submit them to the Ministry of Industry and Commerce for approval and promulgation in accordance with regulations. The meeting adjourned after the discussion.

It is also heard that the Tea Improvement Field, jointly operated by the Central Agricultural Experiment Institute and the Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau, will hold the third Tea Improvement Field Committee meeting at 9 a.m. today at the Central Agricultural Experiment Institute to discuss important matters such as the selection of a successor to the late Director Yu Qian and the plan to reorganize the field's affairs. After receiving the notice, Wu Juenong, a technician from the Agricultural Inspection Group of the bureau, departed last night to attend the meeting.

City Federation Cables Ministry of Finance to Correct the Stamp Tax Bureau's Excessive Fines 157

The Shanghai First Special District Citizen's Federation, believing that the Shanghai Stamp Tax Bureau deliberately imposes excessive fines, disturbing merchants and harming the people, requested the Ministry of Finance to correct it. Yesterday, they sent a telegram to Kong, Minister of the Ministry of Finance of the Executive Yuan of the National Government in Nanjing, stating: "According to a letter from the 27th Branch of the Federation, a member of the association, Quan Xingkang, reported that on the afternoon of the 18th of this month, at 2 p.m., personnel from the Stamp Office went to the shop to inspect the stamps. At that time, they took away twelve books and two folders. However, all the account books of the shop have always been stamped without omission. But the books, etc., taken away were old and defective, some with the covers separated, and some with the stamps missing, not intentionally evading the tax. Now, we specially send a letter to your association, asking you to uphold justice, consider the difficulties of merchants, and negotiate with the Stamp Office to return the books, etc., taken away in full." In view of this, the member has always attached great importance to government tax revenue, and all books that should be affixed with stamp tax have never been evaded. The twelve account books taken away this time are indeed old and defective, and the old stamps inevitably fall off after a long time. We specifically request that you consider the difficulties of merchants and approve a letter to the Special District Stamp Tax Bureau, ordering the immediate return of the account books taken away." The Shanghai Biscuit, Candy, and Canned Food Trade Association also sent a letter stating, "Recently, the Shanghai Stamp Tax Bureau has been very serious about inspecting the stamp affixing of various shops. Even slight errors are punished, which is very harmful to merchants. Those who deliberately fail to affix stamps or affix an insufficient amount of stamps deserve to be punished. However, there are also those who clearly comply with the regulations and affix stamps in accordance with the law, but are fined for no reason due to the inspectors' desire for credit or negligence. Once executed, it is impossible to recover. For example, a receipt of 88 jiao from our member, Dehua Biscuit Company, was affixed with a stamp of 1 fen, but was fined 5 yuan by the Stamp Tax Law Violation Review Committee. After our association went to plead the case, they claimed that it had already been executed and could not be revoked. In addition, a payment notice from Taichang Food Company, in accordance with commercial practice, is merely a simple notice and has no monetary payment relationship. After our association pleaded repeatedly to no avail, it was eventually fined 20 yuan. In view of this, there is no room for redress for those who are wrongly fined. Those who should not be fined are judged according to the mood of the bureau, doing whatever they want, which is difficult to justify. If this trend continues, even loans of friendship or inquiry notes must be affixed with stamps. Lawyers' letters for collecting debts are not seen to be affixed with stamps. Merchants are adding unexpected burdens, which is both funny and sad. In addition to sending a letter to the Review Committee to pay attention, it is generally believed that this type of event is a common problem for the entire business community. All merchants should express their opinions. Therefore, we specifically send a letter to various trade associations, asking for their support and cooperation in resisting this. We also send a letter to your association, hoping that you will propose a discussion to jointly seek a solution to alleviate the suffering. We are very grateful for your assistance. We have learned that the Stamp Tax Inspection Office uses concession police force to arbitrarily oppress Chinese merchants, while condoning foreign merchants who do not affix stamps, which is harmful to the country and the people. We specifically request that you promptly revoke this and correct the various excessive fines of the Shanghai Stamp Tax Bureau. The country will be fortunate, and the merchants will be fortunate. Shanghai First Special District Citizen's Federation." Sincerely, printed.

Shanghai Municipal Council Discusses the Issue of Recruiting Business Corps Members 158

The Business Corps Member Recruitment Committee of the Shanghai Municipal Council, with the consent of the Chairman of the Council, invited representatives of the British and American Chambers of Commerce to the Business Corps gymnasium on the upper floor of the Municipal Council at noon on the 12th to discuss the issue of increasing the number of corps members, with particular emphasis on British and American members. Those present included the British and American Consuls General, the Presidents of the British and American Chambers of Commerce, the Chairman of the Municipal Council, the members of the committee, the Commander of the Business Corps, and the Director-General of the Municipal Council. The meeting was chaired by Mr. Arnold, Chairman of the Committee and Vice-Chairman of the Municipal Council. After the meeting began, the Chairman delivered a speech, stating in essence that according to the report of the Commander of the Business Corps, there are currently more than 800 vacancies in the corps, especially the lack of British and American members, which is a matter of regret. Because Shanghai is in a special position, there have been dangers in the past, and it is necessary to rely on self-defense. Although the foreign troops stationed in Shanghai have historically assisted the Business Corps and the police of this sector in protecting life and property, in view of the recent withdrawal of a battalion of British troops, in the event of an emergency, the existing foreign troops are not sufficient for the first line of defense. The Business Corps must take on the work of the first line, so it must have a sufficient number of people who are properly trained to cope with the situation. In the past, the mobilization of the Business Corps sometimes took too long, which caused inconvenience to businesses due to the lack of personnel. This difficulty has now been planned to be resolved. It is hoped that the leaders of various firms will encourage their young employees to serve, and not think that safety can be expected because there are a few stationed troops. Regarding this matter, it is hoped that various businesses will express their opinions as much as possible. Then, the American Consul General spoke, endorsing the chairman's proposal, hoping that everyone would do their duty. The British Consul General also expressed his full support for this initiative, saying that the British have always been confident and self-reliant, and those who have gone overseas to make a living have always had an active spirit of self-defense. It is the same in Shanghai today, and it is hoped that various businesses will provide their employees with convenience, so that qualified young people will be happy to fulfill their duties. Then, the Commander of the Business Corps stated that he felt the lack of personnel during the last mobilization, and those who joined temporarily were not easy to incorporate, so they must enlist in advance. As for the corps members, there are active duty members and Grade A and B reserve members. Active duty members must go to training at least twelve times a year, excluding inspections and shooting practice. Grade A members go to training six fewer times, and Grade B members are those who have served in the military. After speaking, the celebrities present discussed it, and it was hoped that the main employees in the firms could be exempted from service unless in extremely urgent situations. The chairman then explained that if there are sufficient corps members, those who have difficulty leaving their posts can be exempted from work.

Fujian Exhibitor Dong Kunfan Returns to Shanghai after Participating in the Chicago Expo 159

Mr. Dong Kunfan, the Fujian exhibitor at the Chicago Exposition, returned to Shanghai yesterday from the United States. According to him, more than 30 national pavilions participated in the Chicago Expo, but only a dozen or so won special awards. Chinese lacquerware was originally a famous product, but due to the lack of organization in foreign trade and the inappropriateness of internal manufacturing, it has declined in recent years. Since this exhibition, the United States has regained its faith in it. Tea umbrellas, bronzes, and other items are also welcomed by them. The Huier Orphanage is originally a charitable organization, which is not easy to maintain. With this honor, it is believed that all sectors will provide more support.

The World Red Swastika Society believes that it is necessary to provide relief to refugees and wounded soldiers in the war zones of Zhejiang and Fujian due to the recent conflicts. Meeting Record of the Jisheng Society 162

The Chinese Jisheng Society held a committee meeting yesterday, attended by more than 20 people. Mr. Wang Yiting was publicly elected as the chairman to report on the relief efforts in the 22nd year. It is estimated that two porridge factories were opened in the spring at the Baiyi Convent and Chaoyangmen outside of Beijing, and seeds were transported to Wugong County, Shaanxi, including 1,700 dan of white rice. There was also relief work for the Guangfeng Dike Project in Jiangxi. In the summer, various charitable organizations jointly provided relief for the bandit disaster in Zhengyangguan, Anhui. In the autumn, charitable organizations jointly provided relief for the Yellow River flood disaster in Heze County, Shandong, and the typhoon disaster in Baoshan, Chongming, Chuansha, and Qidong counties. In winter, two porridge factories were opened at the Baiyi Alley and Chaoyangmen outside of Beijing this year. This year, the porridge factories have been changed to rice distribution. In addition, 500 sets of cotton clothes were transported. The total amount spent on medicine throughout the year was approximately 17,000 yuan. The relief work that has not yet been completed is the winter relief work in Fuyang, Taihe, and Yingshang counties of Anhui. Mr. Feng Yangshan, a committee member, was publicly elected to handle it. However, due to bandits everywhere, there was no way to proceed, and he has returned to Shanghai. Now, Mr. Zhang Zefu has also sent a telegram saying that he will arrive in Shanghai immediately to beg for relief. One sluice of the Guangfeng Dike in Jiangxi has not yet been built, the funds for the Beijing porridge factories have not yet been raised, and the funds for the two porridge factories in the local area have not yet been delivered. Then, the number of receipts and expenditures for this year was reported. The total amount of receipts and expenditures for the entire year of the 22nd year was a total of 200,000 yuan, which is only two-thirds of the previous year. The depression situation is rare in previous years, so the disaster relief in various places has not been fully handled. Then, the relief work for this year was proposed. Committee member Feng Yangshan said that there are new wars in Zhejiang and Fujian, and the people who have fled and suffered as a result are especially pitiful. We should prepare to go to provide relief. Although the society does not have preparatory funds, it should call for them as soon as possible. There must be kind people who will rise up upon hearing the news, and it was resolved to pass it. Also, the Yangzhou porridge factory has been operated by the society for two years. This time, Mr. Li Lingsheng sent a letter requesting that the winter relief work continue. It was resolved to pass it. The society has always had a reputation for being realistic and pragmatic in handling relief work. Recently, disasters have been widespread, and the people are crying out for food. Winter relief and spring relief both require funds everywhere. We hope that enthusiastic people will donate generously so that the society can actively carry out its work and benefit the disaster victims.
